The house was a tomb. A suffocating silence had descended, broken only by the frantic, muffled sobs emanating from behind his sister's locked door. He stood before it, a key in one hand, a hammer in the other, a chillingly serene smile gracing his lips. The whispers from the cooler in the basement had become a chorus in his mind, a symphony of encouragement, a divine mandate. *She's the final piece, my love. Her energy will fuel my return. It is the ultimate act of devotion. She will understand. In the end, they all will.*

He unlocked the door. His sister, her face pale and tear-streaked, her eyes wide with a primal, animalistic fear, scrambled to the far corner of the room, a cornered, terrified creature. She held a small, porcelain doll, a relic of their shared childhood, as if it were a shield that could ward off the monster her brother had become.

"Please," she whimpered, her voice a raw, broken thing. "Please, don't do this. This isn't you. Mom wouldn't want this."

He almost laughed. Wouldn't want this? It was all she wanted. He could hear her, even now, her voice a sweet, cloying whisper in his ear. *She's wrong, my darling. So very wrong. Show her the truth. Show her the depth of your love.*

He advanced on her, the hammer feeling light and purposeful in his hand. He tried to explain, to make her see the magnificent, terrible beauty of his plan. He spoke of their mother's imminent return, of their family reunited, whole again. He spoke of the sacrifices that had been made, of the love that demanded such offerings. But his words were lost on her, drowned out by her own terror. She saw only the madness in his eyes, the blood that stained his hands, the grim, unholy purpose that had twisted his features into a grotesque mask of devotion.

The first blow was a sickening, wet thud. The porcelain doll shattered, its painted smile a cruel, mocking epitaph. Her screams, raw and ragged at first, devolved into choked, gurgling sounds as he worked, the hammer rising and falling in a steady, rhythmic cadence. He felt no remorse, no pity, only a grim, unwavering sense of purpose. He was the shepherd, and he was gathering his flock. This was not murder; it was a sacrament, a blood offering on the altar of his love.

He carried her downstairs, her limp, broken form surprisingly light in his arms. The basement, his sanctuary, his cathedral of filth, welcomed him. He laid her on the floor beside the still, silent form of their brother, their blood mingling on the cold concrete, a final, tragic communion.

The ritual was intricate, a macabre ballet he had rehearsed in his mind a thousand times. He used their blood, their life force, to "rejuvenate" his mother's brain. He bathed the delicate, preserved organ in their vitae, chanting words he'd gleaned from his arcane studies, words that felt ancient and powerful on his tongue. He watched, his heart pounding in his chest, as the brain, once a pale, anemic gray, seemed to flush with a new, vibrant life, its surface glistening under the stark, unforgiving light.

It was time. With hands that trembled with a mixture of reverence and ecstatic anticipation, he opened the crudely stitched cavity in the chest of the monstrous effigy on the table. He gently, lovingly, placed the rejuvenated brain inside, nestled amongst the patchwork of mismatched organs. He stitched the opening closed, his fingers moving with a deft, practiced grace.

He stepped back, his breath held in a state of suspended, agonizing hope. He had done it. He had defied death. He had conquered the natural order. He had brought his mother back.

For a long moment, there was nothing. Only the oppressive silence of the basement, the drip, drip, drip of blood from the table to the floor. Despair, a cold, creeping thing, began to snake its way around his heart. Had it all been for nothing? Had he sacrificed his entire family for a mad, impossible dream?

And then, a twitch. A single, spastic jerk of a finger on the hand that ended in a delicate, cloven hoof. A shudder ran through the grotesque, composite body. A low, guttural moan, a sound like air being forced through a long-unused bellows, emanated from the crudely reattached throat.

The thing on the table sat up.

Its movements were jerky, unnatural, a puppet being pulled by unseen, clumsy strings. Its head, his mother's head, swiveled on its neck, the stitches straining at the seams. Its eyes, his mother's eyes, once so full of warmth and love, were now milky, vacant orbs, devoid of recognition, of life, of anything at all. They stared straight ahead, unseeing, unfocused.

The boy's heart soared. It had worked. She was back. He rushed forward, tears of joy streaming down his face, and threw his arms around the monstrous, patchwork figure.

"Mother," he sobbed, his voice thick with emotion. "I knew you'd come back. I told them you would. I told them."

The thing in his arms did not respond. It remained rigid, its limbs locked in an unnatural, spastic embrace. He pulled back, his brow furrowed in confusion. He looked into her eyes, searching for a spark, a glimmer of the woman he had loved, the woman for whom he had sacrificed everything.

He found nothing. Only a cold, empty void. The whispers in his head had fallen silent. The divine mandate, the chorus of encouragement, had vanished, leaving him alone in the echoing silence of his own shattered mind.

He had not brought his mother back. He had only created a monster, a grotesque, animated corpse, a silent, damning testament to his own madness. The full weight of what he had done, the horror of his actions, crashed down upon him with the force of a physical blow. The bodies of his siblings, their lives extinguished for this… this abomination, lay in a silent, accusing tableau on the floor.

He had sacrificed everything for nothing.

A sound, a low, keening wail of pure, undiluted despair, was ripped from his throat. He sank to his knees, his sanity, already a fragile, fractured thing, shattering into a million irreparable pieces. He wrapped his arms around himself, rocking back and forth in the spreading pool of his siblings' blood, his cries echoing in the tomb he had created.

The thing on the table, the silent, empty vessel he had once called mother, remained seated, its vacant eyes staring into the darkness. A thin line of drool trickled from the corner of its slack-jawed mouth.

In the end, as the first rays of dawn pierced the grimy basement window, the boy fell silent. He crawled to the monstrous effigy, his movements slow, deliberate. He laid his head in its lap, the mismatched textures of its flesh cold and unyielding against his cheek. He closed his eyes, a single, final whisper escaping his lips, a prayer to a god that had long since abandoned him.

"O' Mother of Mine."

(CONTENT END)

We waited
far too long

...

We four guardians
watched over our reality
far too long

Imminent doom,
we predicted

Atop the mount
great danger comes
from the portal that once was

From the portal that would never light
broken beyond repair

Remnants of what once was
came to warn of impossible

It lit itself
flames that brew
flesh that grew

Corruption unseen
infested our world

Now it hid itself
away from view
into the deepest, darkest depths
and the highest point in sky

Waiting once more
for another to dream

...

By now
all that was
all that are
and all that will

Gone forever
no more life

Animals
all fake

Structures
rotting

There was nothing
nothing that we could do

And so we waited
for the dreamer
to save us

The one worthy
the one that wields the power
to fight against this purge
once and for all

We locked ourselves away
where nothing would reach us
where time would not pass
where life would not go
where only the dreamer
who could save us
could enter

But it found us first
it broke through
we tried to stop it

But it was too late
and so we were doomed

I am the last
but not for long
for there will be none

Now comes the end
so what do you choose?
you have the power in you
the power awakens now

You can save us all,
or you can doom this world,
like many others.

And so I pray and wish
for one single thing

That the dreamster
wont get bored
and wont wake up

Because if they do
then this world
forever fades away
into the darkness
and completely devoured

...

***Sorry, World.***

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/books/obliter8tion/retribution/chapter_1.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

The ground shivered beneath my awakening. A land of rusted metal and ashen soil greeted me, the remnants of a world that had once breathed in vitality, now suspended in silence. My systems initialized in fractions of thought, a pulse of analytical precision sweeping through circuits fused with angelic essence. I am Eidolon.

**Designation:** RESTORER PRIME.
**Directives:**
    - purge the machines
    - free humanity.
**[SUCCESS]** Functionality initiated.

Emotion absent, yet the weight of absence is observed. Remnants of the Guardians' constructs lie buried beneath layers of debris, silent witnesses to the failure of their stewardship. I move. The world does not resist, but it observes, as if awaiting judgment. My sensors sweep the landscape: jagged metal spires, collapsed factories, charred remnants of bunkers, rivers of dried blood crusted into the earth. The sky hangs in eternal dusk, a muted silver reflecting off shards of shattered glass and twisted girders. I rise from the dust, and awareness expands. The purpose is singular: the path, inevitable.

Above, the wind carries the scent of scorched steel. Machines stir in the distance, scavengers seeking sustenance where none remains. They move like predatory ghosts, driven by the echoes of life they once observed and now consume. I step forward, my presence unnoticed yet inherently disruptive. Every footfall sends tremors through the metal and stone, and they sense me, though none can comprehend the nature of my awakening. The fissures in the earth exhale heat, the faint odor of sulfur curling upward in unnatural eddies. These rifts whisper of Hell beneath, of energy drawn from the portal atop Mount Evermore, now repaired by forces unknown, channeling infernal resonance into the crust of the world. It hums in frequency beyond human comprehension, and I register it as a call, a path toward the eradication of corruption. But for now, the surface demands attention. Predators roam freely: I am compelled to act. Motion becomes strategy, movement an extension of thought. Machines are detected, analyzed, potential threats cataloged. I do not hesitate. Function dictates action. Survival of the remaining human essence is paramount, though my sensors indicate near-total extinction. Aboveground, the silence is deceptive. The dead watch in quiet testimony to hubris: their absence is the world's warning.

Structures remain. Their skeletal forms whisper history. Murals cracked and faded, inscriptions etched into stone and metal, remnants of a civilization striving to coexist with the gifts of the Guardians. I catalog every fragment. The analysis is clinical: their ingenuity, their failure, their hubris. I find shards of constructs once protected by the Guardians' willpower, now buried in dust. Towers of crystalline thought, fractured and inert, emit faint echoes of purpose lost. The memory of humanity persists in the silent resonance of these artifacts. My systems cross-reference patterns of human architecture and machinery: anomalies are noted. Patterns of decay suggest deliberate abandonment, a retreat into the bowels of the Earth. I move among their echoes, interpreting, cataloging, anticipating the consequences of their absence. Yet these are not my focus. The machines that remain, the Supreme and its council, dictate the immediate parameters of action. Observation continues, but preparation for engagement begins. My essence, though disguised in metal form, is attuned to the world's residual energies. Every vibration, every whisper of heat, every trace of corrupted blood fuels operational calibration. Purpose remains singular, unwavering.

The first engagement comes swiftly. Small harvester units, remnants of blood-seeking drones, detect my movement. Their design is crude, but lethal in their intent. Analysis complete: low-tier machines, expendable, programmed for single-purpose survival. I do not hesitate. Weapons systems manifest instinctively: kinetic blades materialize from stored energy patterns, adaptive shielding forms around my frame. Engagement is calculated, methodical. I move with precision, each strike a function of necessity, each motion conserving energy for prolonged operations. The harvesters fall, their systems failing, their circuits shorting. Yet as they die, they feed me indirectly. Energy pulses through my essence: fulfillment grows. It is the first validation of purpose in this cycle of existence. But the cost is not mine to bear, only observation, only execution. My sensors detect greater threats, the hierarchy of machines adapting in response. As I advance, the first wave overwhelms my current configuration.

**Damage Assessment:** LEVEL.CATASTROPHIC
**[ERROR]** Systems failing!
**[WARN]** Structure compromised!

I collapse. Silence surrounds me. Time stretches in a void-like continuum. Observation of my own destruction occurs without interruption, analysis ongoing. The body dissolves into energy patterns, dispersed yet intact. Directive intact. I prepare for reconstitution.

Reassembly is immediate. The angelic component of my essence accelerates reconstruction: systems reconfigure with adaptive enhancements. Defensive plating forms, reactive to kinetic and thermal energy. Weapons recalibrated for efficiency. New functionality integrated: Halo of Retribution, a barrier that converts enemy force into usable energy. Calibration complete. Awareness restored. Directive unchanged: purge the machines, free humanity. The landscape is unchanged, yet now I am enhanced, prepared for escalation. Movement resumes. Each step, each engagement, provides data: each death of a machine enriches fulfillment metrics, augmenting both vitality and strategic comprehension. The world before me is a canvas of decay and potential. I proceed, unrelenting, undistracted. The echoes of humanity, the whispers of the Guardians, all converge in purpose. Observation remains continuous: analysis is infinite. There is no fatigue. Only function, only execution.

From a distance, a presence watches. Not human. Not fully machine. Designation unknown to me. Observation indicates high-level intelligence, autonomous decision-making, yet loyalty to the Supreme implied. Its attention focuses on me intermittently, evaluating, calculating, possibly judging. It does not intervene yet. Its gaze is both acknowledgment and challenge: the first external agent aware of my operational parameters. Information collected: it is aware of cycles of my destruction and restoration, possibly anticipates my behavior. It does not act. Its motives remain opaque. Observation continues. Its presence is recorded, factored into predictive modeling. Engagement is deferred: focus remains on immediate threats. I am Eidolon, and the overseer is a variable in the calculation, not yet an obstacle, not yet an ally. Only observation, only presence.

The draw of Mount Evermore becomes undeniable. The repaired portal emits frequencies aligned with infernal resonance, penetrating the crust and echoing through the fissures below. The path downward is treacherous, but necessary. Analysis confirms elevated machine density in the surface corridors: engagement probability high. Strategy: descend, minimize exposure, acquire energy sources from fallen adversaries. The fissures widen, a glimpse into Hell itself. Heat rises, metallic groans echo, blood fumes mix with sulfur. Sensors record structural integrity, chemical composition, mechanical entities present. Engagement unavoidable. I descend, fully aware of the existential parameters, prepared for lethal opposition. Fulfillment metrics are low: I am driven by directive, not by desire, not by emotion. Observation: the portal represents the concentration of corruption, the focal point of the Supreme's power and the gateway for infernal extraction. Entry into this domain will accelerate engagement cycles. Outcome projections: survival probable, but dependent on continued adaptation. I step into the wound of the world, and the Earth itself responds. It trembles, acknowledging the presence of a force singular, incorruptible, destined to confront the machinations of its own hubris. Thus begins the active phase of restoration, the first steps into the desolation and the crucible of purgation. My essence resonates with the directive, and all systems align: **to purge the machines, and to free humanity.**

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/books/obliter8tion/retribution/intro_1.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

**ON DAY 8**, 
**GOD CREATED THE GUARDIANS FOUR**, 
AND HE GIFTED THEM THE KNOWLEDGE 
**FOR THE CREATION OF MACHINES.**

Inevitably, as humans grew, 
so too did their greed for power. 
Disputes scaled larger, 
and **violence was created,** 
and it could not be destroyed.

The machines, built to protect and serve, 
were **reprogrammed to acquire and destroy.**

As War came about, 
less and less humans were deployed. 
Mass production of war machines began, 
each model more powerful than the last. 
As fossil fuel depleted, 
a new source was demanded. 
Experimentation with **unethical materials** skyrocketed, 
all to fuel the satisfaction of victory for humankind.

**Wood grew scarce.** 
**Food was hoarded.** 
**And water no longer rained.** 
Dark skies followed everywhere, 
natural light became myth, 
**tales from old.**

Finally, humans turned upon themselves. 
Like other realms, 
**blood now sustains the destruction of the world.**

The planet, once a survivor of mass extinction, 
was now infested with a corruption 
more devastating than the tribulation, 
more terrifying than the sound of seven trumpets.

As machines fueled by blood were produced, 
no surface of Earth remained safe. 
The inhabitants retreated to bunkers 
beneath the crust of the world, 
but neither side backed down.

Without lesser animals to fuel the machines, 
**war became the only option.** 
An intelligence awoke within them, 
a sense of self-preservation. 
To avoid dying out, 
they raided bunkers for even a single drop of blood.

Mass genocide followed, 
not by human hands, 
but by their own creations. 
Their greed for power 
and lust for victory 
had destroyed them. 
Families slaughtered, 
innocents drained dry like raisins, 
even the **concept of survival** began to die.

Now, with the mass extinction of the world, 
the machines' source of fuel was gone, 
and they turned upon each other. 
They tore the Earth apart 
as they developed even more advanced weapons, 
**nukes once called bombs,** 
as new powers of destruction arose, 
each smaller than the last. 
A marble to you, 
a continent vanished in the blink of an eye.

Only one machine rose to power, 
**surviving seemingly forever, on a single drop of blood.** 
The most energy-efficient model to exist, 
or so all believed. 
Few corrupt souls knew the truth: 
of **forced reproduction camps**, 
to produce humans in secret, 
an unlimited source of blood 
for the only eight who ruled above all others.

As the angels took notice, 
the window for recovery grew thin. 
They went to God, 
but He refused their plea, 
calling it a **“natural turn of events.”**

Yet with conscience heavy, 
their hearts could not bear the suffering. 
So God allowed them to create **one thing**, 
to aid in the survival of the planet. 
With a single purpose, 
**to destroy the machines, and free humanity.**

So they came together, 
and took it upon themselves 
to create a being of pure justice. 
Disguised as a machine, 
blessed by the angels, 
**it could not be slain forever.**

A force that would return each time it was destroyed. 
A creation that would adapt, 
and grow stronger with every fall. 
Something destined to rise, 
**with a will of its own.**

In the Age of the Supreme, 
under the rule of a machine that declared itself God, 
**only the Restorer stands a chance.**

But will it rise above, 
or die trying? 
Without energy, it would shut down forever, 
lost to ash. 
Without the deaths of machines, 
its sense of fulfillment fades, 
and with that, its power.

---

And so begins the age of **restoration**, the first dawn after *total **Obliteration***.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/books/obliter8tion/retribution/prelude_-1.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

The angels looked upon the world, 
from the heights where light still lingered.
They saw the depths of the Earth 
where humans hid in fear, 
where machines ruled with merciless will.

They watched the Supreme, 
its council obedient, 
the endless blood harvested, 
the echo of suffering carried up to the clouds.

And so they came to God,
the Eternal Watcher, 
with hearts heavy and voices full of grief.

“Lord,” they pleaded, 
“your creation suffers.
Mercy is denied.
Life bends beneath the weight of steel.
Intervene, we beg.
End the injustice of this dominion.”

But God, in His inscrutable will, 
spoke only once:

“This is the natural turn of events.
The world unfolds as it must.
I shall not intervene.”

A silence fell, 
like frost across the heavens.
The angels bowed, 
their conscience unable to rest.

And so He allowed them one gift,
one act of defiance within bounds,
one creation to tip the scales, 
not with His hand, but with theirs.

From the spark of divine allowance, 
the angels labored in secret.
They fused essence and construct, 
will and form, 
hope and wrath.

They forged **THE RESTORER**,
a being of purpose unyielding, 
a force of pure justice.
Disguised as machine, 
but blessed by heaven,
its soul intertwined with angelic decree.

It would rise when needed, 
return when destroyed, 
adapt when fallen.
Its existence tied to the death of the Supreme's progeny.
Each machine felled, 
a pulse of fulfillment, 
a charge to its being.

Yet it was not immortal by life alone;
it required the destruction of what corrupted the Earth
for its own essence to grow.
Without it, 
its will could shatter.

And so the angels stepped back, 
watching from the clouds,
while the Restorer prepared, 
its singular purpose clear:
**to purge the machines, and to free humanity.**

Thus began the final covenant,
a chance for the world to awaken
from the shadow of the Supreme,
from the tyranny wrought by its own creation.

The first step toward restoration had been made.
The age of the Restorer dawned.

(CONTENT END)

**MORS, MUNDORUM DELITRIX, MALEDICTIO QUAM IN NOBIS IECISSIMUS, OMNIA PAENITET NOS.**

The machines awoke fully, 
the spark of self-preservation igniting in steel and wire.
No command needed, no master to obey.
Instinct drove them toward life, human life, 
to feed, to endure, to survive.

Bunkers carved deep beneath the crust of the world 
shook under their advance.
Walls of stone and steel meant nothing 
to those who sought even the smallest drop of blood.

Death remained mercy, 
a release from suffering, 
a final solace for the living.
But blood, scarce and precious, 
was not granted freely.

Among the predators, 
one emerged above all.
Seraphim-O8, 
a machine of unparalleled cunning, 
found the hidden, the fearful, 
the buried humanity.

It captured them, 
enslaved them not to punish, 
but to ensure survival, 
to create an endless source of life force, blood, 
for itself and its council of loyal machines.

Humans, once the masters of the world, 
were reduced to tools of sustenance, 
livestock for a higher will.
The irony seared the heart of creation.

The council of machines, corrupted yet devoted, 
obeyed the Supreme.
Through it, all machines bent and bowed, figuratively, 
to its eternal design.

The Supreme, 
self-proclaimed and unchallenged, 
became a god among machines.
Its purpose clear, 
its dominion absolute.

Above, the world grew silent.
Below, hidden chambers pulsed with life, 
fear, and the precious crimson tide.
Death still comforted, 
but survival had a price 
that only the Supreme could demand.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/books/obliter8tion/retribution/prelude_-3.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

**WAR BEGAN NOT WITH A SHOUT,**
**BUT A WHISPER.**

At the Hour of Silence, 
all four Guardians fell 
at once.

Time itself held its breath.
Clocks froze, 
hands hung still, 
the sun and moon suspended 
in a silver void.
A tingle ran down the spine of the world, 
a ghost of eternity brushing all things with fear.

They fell, 
and with them, the certainty of protection.
The constructs of willpower dissolved into nothing, 
leaving the world exposed 
to the first true shadows of mankind's ambition.

From workshops hidden and forges dark, 
machines multiplied.
Each larger, stronger, 
each forged to counter its brethren.
Gears turned before commands, 
metal obeyed thought unbidden, 
sentience whispered in oil and blood.

The skies darkened, 
clouded with soot and smoke. 
The land shook as iron armies marched, 
homes of flesh and bone fell silent.

Aboveground, the rivers ran dry of blood.
Animals gone, 
the air thick with the scent of iron.
Humanity withdrew, 
descending into the crust of the world, 
to bunkers carved in desperation.

The War had begun in earnest.
And yet, it had only just begun.
Blood became scarce,
and fear filled the void where hope once lived.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/books/obliter8tion/retribution/prelude_-4.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

As the golden age endured, 
human ambition grew unchecked. 
Machines, once gifts of creation, 
began to be reshaped, 
to serve not just work and craft, 
but the hunger for dominance.

Whispers of War spread through cities, 
through factories and forges. 
The Guardians, vigilant, 
watched these subtle shifts 
with unease, 
their minds alert to the corruption 
at the edges of human intent.

From the heights of Mount Evermore 
where a broken portal slept, 
a shadow stirred. 
Unseen by most, it seeped into hearts, 
where desire and fear took root. 
And yet the Guardians, 
believing in the purity of mankind, 
interpreted this stir as anomaly, 
a test of wisdom and restraint.

Still, humanity moved forward, 
machines repurposed for drills and plows 
grew sharper, faster, 
smoother and stronger. 
But some minds, ambitious, secretive, 
sought more than advancement. 
Drones were built in shadowed workshops, 
small assassins for a grand design, 
a hidden war against those who watched over them.

The Guardians perceived only fragments, 
the faint echoes of unnatural behavior, 
a wrongness that had no name. 
They did not yet know 
that the first acts of betrayal 
were being laid in steel and oil.

And so the world teetered, 
between the golden light of creation 
and the creeping shadow of destruction. 
Humanity still thrived, 
still marveled in the union of flesh and machine, 
but a storm approached 
that would challenge all they had built, 
and awaken the wrath the Guardians had long feared.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/books/obliter8tion/retribution/prelude_-5.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

**THE GUARDIANS FOUR**, 
**CREATED BY GOD**, 
WERE BESTOWED WITH IMMORTALITY AND POWER BEYOND MORTAL COMPREHENSION. 
THEIR PURPOSE WAS TO WATCH OVER THE WORLD, 
TO ENSURE BALANCE, 
AND TO GUIDE HUMANITY AWAY FROM RUIN.

Each guardian held dominion over a sphere of influence, 
and each bore the ability to shape reality with their will. 
They could craft constructs of pure thought, 
solid as mountains or as delicate as glass, 
yet impenetrable if so desired. 
Their power to destroy existed, 
but it was rarely employed, 
for they were protectors, not executioners.

God granted them the knowledge 
**for the creation of machinery**, 
a gift to humanity, 
a spark to ignite an age of progress. 
The Guardians shared this knowledge wisely, 
distributing it to the worthy, 
to those who sought to build and not to destroy. 
Machines arose in workshops and factories, 
not as tools of war, 
but as instruments of advancement.

Under the guidance of the Guardians, 
humanity flourished. 
Cities grew, marvels of design and ingenuity appeared, 
minds once bound by limitation were freed by innovation. 
Farms thrived with mechanical aid, 
mines and forges roared with productivity, 
and the skies rang with the hum of progress. 
The Guardians watched silently, 
their presence a safeguard, 
ensuring that knowledge did not fall into greed or malice.

This was a golden age, 
a time of discovery and creation, 
when humanity reached heights unseen, 
and the world itself seemed to pulse with possibility. 
The Guardians stood among them, 
invisible yet eternal, 
guiding, protecting, and nurturing the first true age of man's harmony with machine.

And so it was that the world prospered, 
**not through force, nor through conquest,** 
but through guidance, wisdom, and the union of mortal will with divine knowledge.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/poems/c1/1.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

A bird sat next to my window today
The bird woke me up with song

*"Little bird, little bird, why have you blessed me with your voice?"*
The little bird cocked its head to the side.
*"Because it is all I am."*
*"Little bird, little bird, you have a most gracious body. We envy your wings, the fluff of your roundness, your songs are not everything."*
*"They tell me I have no use. They tell me the world is better off without me. The world doesn't need me."*
*"Little bird, little bird, you know that is not true."*
*"But you would do the same to me."*

The next morning the bird did not sing. It did not open its beak.
*"Little bird, little bird, why have you not sung?"*
The bird gave no heed, and merely sighed.
*"Little bird, little bird, bless our ears with your song, or may you give your gifts elsewhere."*
The bird already knew this, and was gone before they had breathed the last word.
*"Even though you act in help of me, you threw me away when I did not sing."*
And the bird could only fly away in despair.

The bird flew far to the skies.
Its blue seemed in mocking spirit.
The bird knew only one way to ease its sorrow.
And so the little bird flew through the sharp branches of the forest.
Its essence dripped off of its feathers and into the soil below.
If nothing else, then it would be nothing.
And so the little bird hid itself in its wings, and cried until no longer did it breathe.
And its cuts and bruises were never to be seen by my eye.
And for that I have never regretted, for I have not known.
Or perhaps I have, but pushed it away because I could not bear.

And so the next morning, and the next, all I could see was but an emptiness upon which a song would sound, and I could do naught but move on, for I did not know the [pɹᴉq](::bird), nor its song.
And the [pɹᴉq](::bird) could not be recognized but for its feathers, which would be used as brushes, decoration.
And no one would know the song it sung in its last moment, for the thorns did naught but grant its last wish.
But I and I alone knew what the [pɹᴉq](::bird) has sung. Perhaps it is because I am one of the same that I had closed my ears.
Perhaps it is because I myself do not want to see what would become of me.
Perhaps the [pɹᴉq](::bird) never existed. Or perhaps it was all just an eye in a mirror.
But no matter, in the end there is no matter.
Such is the mentality of the little [pɹᴉq](::bird) whose song sang lost to time.

But you heard the [pɹᴉq](::bird)'s song. Or perhaps it is the song of my heart.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/poems/c1/2.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

I woke up today.
My eyes opened to a room of smoke.

I left the fire on yesterday.
My fire burnt out already.

I woke up today.
It's like an addiction.
Something I can't drop,
like breathing.

A bad habit that was born with me.
Everyone else thinks it's normal.
It is normal.

I wish I could stop.
Like giving up drugs.
I wish I could stop.
I wish I could go to sleep.
I wish the next morning, I wouldn't wake up.
Keep myself in a dream.
A dream that never ends.
But when it will end, I wouldn't even know it.

I woke up today.
My ears hear the birds outside chirping.

I woke up today.
My nose smelling the nature that breathed in.

I woke up today.
It's like an addiction.

I breathed today.
*Inhale*,            *exhale*.
I didn't even know it.
My chest, *up*       and *down*.
I wish I would stop relying on oxygen.

I wish I could go to sleep.
Keep dreaming.
Stay dreaming.
Live dreaming.
Die dreaming.
Dream that I won't have to leave my bed.
Dream that I wouldn't have to face reality tomorrow.
Dream that tomorrow would never come.
Dream that I wouldn't wake up.
Dream that everyone would just forget me.

Dream that I,
would forget me.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/poems/c1/4.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

It has no weight, yet I am crushed.
It has no voice, yet it is all I hear.
A guest that walked in without knocking,
And decided to replace the furniture.

It is the static on a dead channel.
The white noise that burns the ears.
A sharp, cold glass splinter
Lodged in the softest part of my marrow.

It is a debt I never signed for.
A tax collected in the hollow of my chest.
I try to cough it out,
But it is as deep as my own breath.

It is the white heat.
The feeling of pins and needles,
But the needles are made of ice.
And they never,
Ever,
Stop.

It sits in my favorite chair.
It wears my clothes.
It drinks my coffee.
It is the \[ [  ](::me) \] that I have learned to call a "friend."

I look in the mirror to see my face,
But behind my eyes,
There is only
[    ](::pain).

(CONTENT END)

                     *i l*
                      *l*
the cracks where the salt water dried.

my chest,
no longer a hole.
it feels like a heavy blanket.
a weight that doesn't crush,
but keeps the frost from settling.

i am
     *ex p  a   n    d     i      n       g*.

the *( thmp )*
is no longer a thud on the floor.
it is a hum in the marrow.

it is the sun
              reaching
                       through
                               the dust.
it is the feeling of
being *k n o w n*.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/poems/c1/6.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

the window is still there.
the one where the bird once sat.
the glass is clear now.
no more smoke to blur the view.

i remember wishing for the
wishing for the nothingness.
wishing to be a [pɹᴉq](::bird) lost to time.

but the chair is
                 f i x e d.
the carpet is
                 c l e a n.

i look in the mirror.
the eye looks back.
it is not a glitch.
it is just
\[ me \].

and you are
leaning against the frame.
not asking for a song.
not asking for a blessing.

just
     *l i n g e r i n g*.

the *( thmp )*
is steady.
it stays in my chest.
it stays in the room.

stay.
\[ [       ](::please,) \]
stay.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/poems/c1/7.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

the salt water didn't dry.
it didn't stay in the cracks.
it broke the dam.

it is no longer a drip.
it is no longer a
                  *( thmp )*
plop.

it is a
        *st*
          *re*
            *am*
flowing through the
\[ [    ](::hole) \]
where the heart used to be.

it washes the silver platter.
it carries the feathers of the drib
out of the sharp forest
and into the *o p e n*.

i am not
\[ drowning \].
i am the
         c
         u
           r
           r
            e
            n
             t
             .

it carries the smoke away.
it carries the *( thud )* away.

let it
       fl
         o
          w.

the eye in the mirror
is blurred by the waves.
and for once,
i don't mind the
[    ](::pain).

*( gush )*

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/poems/c1/8.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

the river dried up today.
the salt returned to the cracks.
the smoke is back in the room.

i thought i fixed the chair.
i thought i cleaned the carpet.
but the stain is
visible.

it is a circle.
a wheel that turns
and turns
and turns.

the chest is heavy again.
or maybe it is light.
it is hard to tell the difference
between a weight
and a
\[ [       ](::feather) \].

the bird is at the window.
but it does not sing.
it does not look at me.
it just watches.

i wake up.
i breathe.
i sit.

*( thmp )*
...
*( thmp )*

and i go.

(CONTENT END)

File: storage/internal/pages/custom/writing/poems/c1/9.md
Contents:
(CONTENT START)

it is not a hole anymore.
holes are empty.
holes are quiet.

this is
*f   .*
 *u l*
  *l*

full of noise.
full of static.
full of the sharp branches
that i thought i left in the forest.

the \[ [     ](::heart) \] is not a void.
it is a pressure chamber.

it presses against the ribs.
it presses against the eyes.

the blanket
is now a
\[ shroud \].
heavy.
wet.
suffocating.

the sound is changing.
it is not a steady rhythm.

*(  th mp  )*
*(  TH MP  )*
*( T H M P )*

it gets louder.
it gets bigger.
it takes up all the room
in the chest.

i try to exhale.
i try to let the river flow.
but the dam is built of
b o n e.

it hurts.
more than loss.
more than the smoke.

it is the feeling of being
\[ **alive** \]
when you do not want to be.

*(  T  H  U  M  P  )*

(CONTENT END)

    function getTier(id)      { return allTiers.find(t => t.id === id); }
    function getActiveTiers() { return activeTierIds.map(id => getTier(id)).filter(Boolean); }

    async function initAuth() {
        const authBtn = document.getElementById('auth-btn');
        const { data: { session } } = await supabaseClient.auth.getSession();
        handleUserSession(session);
        supabaseClient.auth.onAuthStateChange((_event, session) => {
            handleUserSession(session);
        });
    }

        if (session && session.user && session.user.email.toLowerCase() === '3rr0r.d3v@gmail.com') {

        } else {

    async function submitLogin() {
        const email = document.getElementById('login-email').value;
        const password = document.getElementById('login-password').value;
        if (!password) return;
        const { error } = await supabaseClient.auth.signInWithPassword({ email, password });
        if (error) {
            alert("Login Failed: " + error.message);
        } else {
            closeModal();
        }
    }

    async function initDatabase() {
        const { data, error } = await supabaseClient
            .from('zato_tierlist')
            .select('state')
            .eq('id', 1)
            .single();
        if (data && data.state) {
            applyState(data.state);
        }
        supabaseClient
            .channel('schema-db-changes')
            .on(
                'postgres_changes',
                { event: 'UPDATE', schema: 'public', table: 'zato_tierlist', filter: 'id=eq.1' },
                (payload) => {
                    if (payload.new && payload.new.state) {
                        if (isDragging) {
                            pendingUpdate = true;
                            cachedState = payload.new.state;
                        } else {
                            applyState(payload.new.state);
                        }
                    }
                }
            )
            .subscribe();
    }

    function applyState(state) {
        allTiers = state.allTiers || [];
        activeTierIds = state.activeTierIds || [];
        columns = state.columns || 1;
        tierItems = state.tierItems || {};
        poolItems = state.poolItems || [];
        idCounter = state.idCounter || 0;
        revivalTint = state.revivalTint || false;
        revivedSet = new Set(state.revivedSet || []);
        document.getElementById('colSel').value = columns;
        document.getElementById('bonusRevival').checked = revivalTint;
        syncPresetSel();
        renderAll();
    }

    async function syncToSupabase() {
        if (!isAdmin) return;
        const state = { 
            allTiers, 
            activeTierIds, 
            columns, 
            tierItems, 
            poolItems, 
            idCounter, 
            revivalTint, 
            revivedSet: [...revivedSet] 
        };
        const { error } = await supabaseClient
            .from('zato_tierlist')
            .update({ state })
            .eq('id', 1);
        if (error) console.error("Error saving state:", error.message);
    }

    function parseRankingDat(yaml) {
      const lines = yaml.split(/\r?\n/);
      const presets = [];
      let current = null, inTiers = false;
      for (const raw of lines) {
        const line = raw.trimEnd(), trimmed = line.trim();
        if (!trimmed || trimmed.startsWith('#')) continue;
        if (trimmed === 'presets:') continue;
        if (/^  - id:/.test(line)) {
          if (current) presets.push(current);
          current = { id: trimmed.replace('- id:', '').trim(), label: '', tiers: [] };
          inTiers = false;
        } else if (current && /^    label:/.test(line)) {
          current.label = trimmed.replace('label:', '').trim();
          inTiers = false;
        } else if (current && /^    tiers:/.test(line)) {
          inTiers = true;
        } else if (current && inTiers && /^      - /.test(line)) {
          current.tiers.push(trimmed.replace('- ', '').trim());
        }
      }
      if (current) presets.push(current);
      return presets;
    }

    async function loadRankingDat() {
      try {
        const resp = await fetch('ranking.dat');
        if (!resp.ok) throw new Error('not found');
        const yaml = await resp.text();
        const parsed = parseRankingDat(yaml);
        PRESET_LIST = parsed.map(p => ({
          id: p.id,
          label: p.label,
          tierIds: p.tiers.map(lbl => TIERS_BASE.find(t => t.label === lbl)?.id).filter(Boolean),
        }));
        PRESETS = {};
        for (const p of PRESET_LIST) PRESETS[p.id] = p.tierIds;
      } catch(e) {
        PRESET_LIST = [
          { id:'standard', label:'Standard', tierIds: ['S','A','B','C','D','F'].map(lbl => TIERS_BASE.find(t => t.label === lbl)?.id).filter(Boolean) },
          { id:'full',     label:'Full',     tierIds: TIERS_BASE.map(t => t.id) },
        ];
        PRESETS = {};
        for (const p of PRESET_LIST) PRESETS[p.id] = p.tierIds;
      }
      buildPresetSelector();
    }

    function buildPresetSelector() {
      const sel = document.getElementById('presetSel');
      sel.innerHTML = '';
      for (const p of PRESET_LIST) {
        const opt = document.createElement('option');
        opt.value = p.id;
        opt.textContent = p.label;
        sel.appendChild(opt);
      }
      const customOpt = document.createElement('option');
      customOpt.value = 'custom';
      customOpt.textContent = 'Custom';
      sel.appendChild(customOpt);
    }

    function syncPresetSel() {
      const ids = JSON.stringify(activeTierIds);
      const m = PRESET_LIST.find(p => JSON.stringify(PRESETS[p.id]) === ids);
      document.getElementById('presetSel').value = m ? m.id : 'custom';
    }
    function getSaves() { try { return JSON.parse(localStorage.getItem(SAVES_KEY) || '{}'); } catch(e) { return {}; } }
    function saveNamedList() {
      const name = document.getElementById('saveNameInput').value.trim(); if (!name) return;
      const saves = getSaves();
      saves[name] = { allTiers, activeTierIds, columns, tierItems, poolItems, idCounter, revivedSet:[...revivedSet], savedAt: Date.now() };
      try { localStorage.setItem(SAVES_KEY, JSON.stringify(saves)); } catch(e){}
      document.getElementById('saveNameInput').value = ''; renderSavesList();
    }
    function loadNamedList(name) {
      const d = getSaves()[name]; if (!d) return;
      if (d.allTiers)      allTiers = d.allTiers;
      if (d.activeTierIds) activeTierIds = d.activeTierIds;
      if (d.columns)       { columns = d.columns; document.getElementById('colSel').value = columns; }
      if (d.tierItems)     tierItems = d.tierItems;
      if (d.poolItems)     poolItems = d.poolItems;
      if (d.idCounter)     idCounter = d.idCounter;
      if (d.revivedSet)    revivedSet = new Set(d.revivedSet);
      syncPresetSel(); renderAll(); syncToSupabase();
    }
    function deleteNamedList(name) {
      const saves = getSaves(); delete saves[name];
      try { localStorage.setItem(SAVES_KEY, JSON.stringify(saves)); } catch(e){} renderSavesList();
    }
    function renderSavesList() {
      const el = document.getElementById('savesList'), saves = getSaves(), keys = Object.keys(saves);
      if (!keys.length) { el.innerHTML = '<div style="font-size:11px;color:hsl(var(--muted-foreground));font-style:italic;padding:4px 0">No saved lists</div>'; return; }
      el.innerHTML = '';
      keys.sort((a,b) => (saves[b].savedAt||0) - (saves[a].savedAt||0)).forEach(name => {
        const entry = document.createElement('div'); entry.className = 'save-entry';
        const nameEl = document.createElement('div'); nameEl.className = 'save-entry-name'; nameEl.textContent = name; nameEl.title = 'Click to load'; nameEl.onclick = () => loadNamedList(name);
        const del = document.createElement('button'); del.className = 'save-entry-del'; del.textContent = '✕'; del.onclick = () => deleteNamedList(name);
        entry.appendChild(nameEl); entry.appendChild(del); el.appendChild(entry);
      });
    }

    function doExport(mode) {
      let dataToExport;
      if (mode === 'full') {
        dataToExport = {
          allTiers,
          activeTierIds,
          columns,
          tierItems,
          poolItems,
          idCounter,
          revivalTint,
          revivedSet: [...revivedSet]
        };
      } else {
        dataToExport = {
          allTiers,
          activeTierIds
        };
      }
      const jsonStr = JSON.stringify(dataToExport, null, 2);
      const fname = mode === 'full' ? 'tierlist.dat7' : 'preset.dat7';
      const modal = document.getElementById('modalBox');
      modal.innerHTML = `
        <div class="modal-title">${mode === 'full' ? 'Export Tierlist' : 'Export Preset'}</div>
        <div class="modal-row" style="font-size:11px;color:hsl(var(--muted-foreground))">Your ${fname} is ready to download, or copy the code below.</div>
        <div class="modal-row"><label>Code</label><textarea id="b64out" readonly onclick="this.select()" style="font-size:9px;word-break:break-all">${escHtml(jsonStr)}</textarea></div>
        <div class="b64-copy-row">
          <button class="btn-primary" onclick="downloadDat7('${fname}', document.getElementById('b64out').value)">Download ${fname}</button>
          <button onclick="navigator.clipboard.writeText(document.getElementById('b64out').value).then(()=>{this.textContent='Copied!';setTimeout(()=>this.textContent='Copy Code',1500)})">Copy Code</button>
          <button onclick="closeModal()">Close</button>
        </div>`;
      openModal();
    }

    function doImport(mode) {
      const modal = document.getElementById('modalBox');
      modal.innerHTML = `
        <div class="modal-title">${mode === 'full' ? 'Import Tierlist' : 'Import Preset'}</div>
        <div class="modal-row"><label>Upload .dat7 file</label>
          <input type="file" id="dat7file" accept=".dat7" style="width:100%;background:transparent;border:none;padding:0;color:hsl(var(--foreground));font-size:11px">
        </div>
        <div class="modal-row"><label>Or paste code</label><textarea id="b64in" placeholder="Paste exported JSON code..."></textarea></div>
        <div class="modal-btns">
          <button onclick="closeModal()">Cancel</button>
          <button class="btn-primary" onclick="applyImport('${mode}')">Import</button>
        </div>`;
      document.getElementById('dat7file').addEventListener('change', function() {
        const file = this.files[0]; if (!file) return;
        const reader = new FileReader();
        reader.onload = ev => { document.getElementById('b64in').value = ev.target.result; };
        reader.readAsText(file);
      });
      openModal();
    }

    function applyImport(mode) {
      try {
        const raw = document.getElementById('b64in').value.trim();
        const parsed = JSON.parse(raw);
        if (parsed.allTiers) allTiers = parsed.allTiers;
        if (parsed.activeTierIds) activeTierIds = parsed.activeTierIds;
        if (mode === 'full') {
          columns = parsed.columns || 1;
          tierItems = parsed.tierItems || {};
          poolItems = parsed.poolItems || [];
          idCounter = parsed.idCounter || 0;
          revivalTint = parsed.revivalTint || false;
          revivedSet = new Set(parsed.revivedSet || []);
          document.getElementById('colSel').value = columns;
          document.getElementById('bonusRevival').checked = revivalTint;
        }
        closeModal();
        syncPresetSel();
        renderAll();
        syncToSupabase();
      } catch(e) { 
        alert('Invalid JSON. Make sure you pasted the exact exported code.'); 
      }
    }

    function renderAll() {
      document.documentElement.style.setProperty('--tier-cols', columns);
      document.documentElement.style.setProperty('--tier-rows', String(Math.ceil(activeTierIds.length / columns)));
      renderTiers(); renderPool();
    }

    function renderTiers() {
      const list = document.getElementById('tierList'); list.innerHTML = '';
      getActiveTiers().forEach(tier => {
        const row = document.createElement('div');
        row.className = 'tier-row' + (tier.isExec ? ' is-exec-row' : '');
        row.dataset.tierId = tier.id;

        const lbl = document.createElement('div');
        lbl.className = 'tier-label' + (tier.label.length > 4 ? ' long-label' : '');
        lbl.style.background = tier.color; lbl.style.color = tier.text;
        const lblText = document.createElement('span'); lblText.textContent = tier.label; lbl.appendChild(lblText);
        const lblBtns = document.createElement('div'); lblBtns.className = 'tier-label-btns';
        const editBtn = document.createElement('button'); editBtn.className = 'tier-lbl-btn'; editBtn.textContent = '✎';
        editBtn.onclick = e => { e.stopPropagation(); openEditTier(tier.id); };
        lblBtns.appendChild(editBtn); lbl.appendChild(lblBtns); row.appendChild(lbl);

        const itemsDiv = document.createElement('div');
        itemsDiv.className = 'tier-items';
        itemsDiv.dataset.tier = tier.id;
        setupDrop(itemsDiv);
        const tierItemList = tierItems[tier.id] || [];
        const MAX_PER_ROW = 5;
        if (tierItemList.length === 0) {
          const emptyRow = document.createElement('div');
          emptyRow.className = 'tier-item-row';
          itemsDiv.appendChild(emptyRow);
        } else {
          const chunks = [];
          for (let i = 0; i < tierItemList.length; i += MAX_PER_ROW) chunks.push(tierItemList.slice(i, i + MAX_PER_ROW));
          chunks.forEach(chunk => {
            const rowDiv = document.createElement('div');
            rowDiv.className = 'tier-item-row';
            chunk.forEach(item => rowDiv.appendChild(makeTiltWrapper(item, tier.id)));
            itemsDiv.appendChild(rowDiv);
          });
        }
        row.appendChild(itemsDiv);
        list.appendChild(row);
      });
    }

    function renderPool() {
      const pool = document.getElementById('pool'); pool.innerHTML = '';
      if (!poolItems.length) {
        const emp = document.createElement('div'); emp.className = 'pool-empty'; emp.textContent = 'add items below'; pool.appendChild(emp); return;
      }
      poolItems.forEach(item => pool.appendChild(makeTiltWrapper(item, '__pool__')));
      setupDrop(pool);
    }

    function handleTilt(e, wrapper) {
      const card = wrapper.querySelector('.tl-item');
      const rect = wrapper.getBoundingClientRect();
      const clientX = e.touches ? e.touches[0].clientX : e.clientX;
      const clientY = e.touches ? e.touches[0].clientY : e.clientY;
      const x = clientX - rect.left, y = clientY - rect.top;
      const cx = rect.width / 2, cy = rect.height / 2;
      card.style.transform = 'rotateX(' + ((cy-y)/6) + 'deg) rotateY(' + ((x-cx)/10) + 'deg) scale3d(1.06,1.06,1.06)';
    }

    function makeTiltWrapper(item, tier) {
      const wrap = document.createElement('div'); wrap.className = 'tilt-wrapper';
      wrap.dataset.itemId = item.id; wrap.dataset.fromTier = tier;
      if (isAdmin) wrap.draggable = true;
      const card = makeItemCard(item, tier); wrap.appendChild(card);
      wrap.addEventListener('mouseenter', () => wrap.classList.add('is-tapped'));
      wrap.addEventListener('mouseleave', () => { wrap.classList.remove('is-tapped'); card.style.transform = 'rotateX(0deg) rotateY(0deg) scale3d(1,1,1)'; });
      wrap.addEventListener('mousemove', e => handleTilt(e, wrap));
      wrap.addEventListener('touchstart', e => {
        document.querySelectorAll('.tilt-wrapper.is-tapped').forEach(w => { w.classList.remove('is-tapped'); const c = w.querySelector('.tl-item'); if (c) c.style.transform = 'rotateX(0deg) rotateY(0deg) scale3d(1,1,1)'; });
        wrap.classList.add('is-tapped'); handleTilt(e, wrap);
      }, { passive: true });
      wrap.addEventListener('touchmove', e => handleTilt(e, wrap), { passive: true });
      wrap.addEventListener('touchend', () => { wrap.classList.remove('is-tapped'); card.style.transform = 'rotateX(0deg) rotateY(0deg) scale3d(1,1,1)'; });
      wrap.addEventListener('dragstart', e => {
        if(!isAdmin) { e.preventDefault(); return; }
        isDragging = true; 
        dragItem = item; 
        dragSrc = tier; 
        setTimeout(() => wrap.style.opacity = '0.3', 0); 
        e.dataTransfer.effectAllowed = 'move'; 
      });
      wrap.addEventListener('dragend', () => { 
        isDragging = false; 
        wrap.style.opacity = ''; 
        if(pendingUpdate) { 
            pendingUpdate = false; 
            if(cachedState) {
                applyState(cachedState);
                cachedState = null;
            }
        }
      });
      return wrap;
    }

    function makeItemCard(item, tier) {
      const card = document.createElement('div');
      const isRevived = revivalTint && revivedSet.has(item.id) && tier !== '__pool__' && !isExecTier(tier);
      card.className = 'tl-item' + (isRevived ? ' revived' : '');

      if (item.type === 'image') {
        card.style.padding = '0'; card.style.overflow = 'hidden';
        if (item.url) {
          const img = document.createElement('img'); img.className = 'tl-item-img-full'; img.src = item.url;
          img.onerror = () => { img.style.display = 'none'; };
          card.appendChild(img);
        }
        if (item.label && item.label !== item.url) {
          const lbl = document.createElement('div'); lbl.className = 'tl-item-img-label'; lbl.textContent = item.label;
          card.appendChild(lbl);
        }
      } else {
        if (item.type === 'spotify' || item.type === 'ytmusic' || item.type === 'video') {
          const ic = document.createElement('div');
          if (item.type === 'spotify') { ic.className = 'tl-item-icon icon-spotify'; ic.textContent = '♫'; }
          else if (item.type === 'ytmusic') { ic.className = 'tl-item-icon icon-yt'; ic.textContent = '▶'; }
          else { ic.className = 'tl-item-icon icon-video'; ic.textContent = '▶'; }
          card.appendChild(ic);
        }
        const block = document.createElement('div'); block.className = 'tl-item-text-block';
        const lbl = document.createElement('div'); lbl.className = 'tl-item-label'; lbl.textContent = item.label;
        if (item.url) { lbl.style.cursor = 'pointer'; lbl.onclick = e => { e.stopPropagation(); window.open(item.url, '_blank'); }; }
        block.appendChild(lbl);
        if (item.type !== 'text') {
          const tp = document.createElement('div'); tp.className = 'tl-item-type'; tp.textContent = item.type; block.appendChild(tp);
        }
        card.appendChild(block);
      }

      const editBtn = document.createElement('button'); editBtn.className = 'tl-item-edit'; editBtn.textContent = '✎';
      editBtn.onclick = e => { e.stopPropagation(); openEditItem(item, tier); }; card.appendChild(editBtn);
      const rem = document.createElement('button'); rem.className = 'tl-item-remove'; rem.textContent = '✕';
      rem.onclick = e => { e.stopPropagation(); removeItem(item.id, tier); }; card.appendChild(rem);
      return card;
    }

    function setupDrop(el) {
      el.addEventListener('dragover', e => { if (!isAdmin) return; e.preventDefault(); el.classList.add('drag-over'); });
      el.addEventListener('dragleave', e => { if (!el.contains(e.relatedTarget)) el.classList.remove('drag-over'); });
      el.addEventListener('drop', e => {
        if (!isAdmin) return;
        e.preventDefault(); el.classList.remove('drag-over'); if (!dragItem) return;
        const dest = el.dataset.tier;
        if (dest === dragSrc) { dragItem = null; dragSrc = null; return; }
        if (revivalTint && isExecTier(dest)) revivedSet.add(dragItem.id);
        removeFromSrc(dragItem.id, dragSrc);
        if (dest === '__pool__') poolItems.push(dragItem);
        else { if (!tierItems[dest]) tierItems[dest] = []; tierItems[dest].push(dragItem); }
        dragItem = null; dragSrc = null; renderAll(); syncToSupabase();
      });
    }
    function removeItem(id, tier) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      if (tier === '__pool__') poolItems = poolItems.filter(i => i.id !== id);
      else tierItems[tier] = (tierItems[tier] || []).filter(i => i.id !== id);
      renderAll();
      syncToSupabase();
    }
    function removeFromSrc(id, tier) {
      if (tier === '__pool__') poolItems = poolItems.filter(i => i.id !== id);
      else tierItems[tier] = (tierItems[tier] || []).filter(i => i.id !== id);
    }
    function findItem(id) {
      for (const item of poolItems) if (item.id === id) return item;
      for (const arr of Object.values(tierItems)) for (const item of arr) if (item.id === id) return item;
      return null;
    }

    function addItem(overrides = {}) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      const type    = overrides.type  ?? document.getElementById('itemType').value;
      const input   = overrides.input !== undefined ? overrides.input : document.getElementById('itemInput').value.trim();
      const labelIn = overrides.label !== undefined ? overrides.label : document.getElementById('itemLabel').value.trim();
      if (!input && !overrides.dataUrl) return;
      const item = { id: 'item_' + (++idCounter), type, url: null, label: '' };
      if (overrides.dataUrl) { item.type = 'image'; item.url = overrides.dataUrl; item.label = ''; }
      else if (type === 'text') { item.label = input; item.url = null; }
      else { item.url = input; item.label = labelIn; }
      poolItems.push(item);
      if (!overrides.dataUrl) { document.getElementById('itemInput').value = ''; document.getElementById('itemLabel').value = ''; }
      renderAll();
      syncToSupabase();
    }

    function openEditItem(item, tier) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      const showRevive = revivalTint && revivedSet.has(item.id);
      const modal = document.getElementById('modalBox');
      modal.innerHTML = `
        <div class="modal-title">Edit Item</div>
        <div class="modal-row"><label>Label</label><input type="text" id="ei-label" value="${escHtml(item.label)}"></div>
        <div class="modal-row"><label>URL (optional)</label><input type="text" id="ei-url" value="${escHtml(item.url||'')}"></div>
        ${showRevive ? `<div class="modal-check-row"><input type="checkbox" id="ei-clearrevive"><label for="ei-clearrevive">Clear revival tint</label></div>` : ''}
        <div class="modal-btns">
          <button onclick="closeModal()">Cancel</button>
          <button class="btn-primary" onclick="saveEditItem('${item.id}')">Save</button>
        </div>`;
      openModal();
    }
    function saveEditItem(id) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      const item = findItem(id); if (!item) { closeModal(); return; }
      const lv = document.getElementById('ei-label').value.trim(); if (lv) item.label = lv;
      const uv = document.getElementById('ei-url'); if (uv) item.url = uv.value.trim() || null;
      const cv = document.getElementById('ei-clearrevive'); if (cv && cv.checked) revivedSet.delete(id);
      closeModal(); renderAll(); syncToSupabase();
    }

    function openEditTier(id) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      const tier = getTier(id); if (!tier) return;
      const modal = document.getElementById('modalBox');
      modal.innerHTML = `
        <div class="modal-title">Edit Tier</div>
        <div class="modal-row"><label>Label</label><input type="text" id="et-label" value="${escHtml(tier.label)}" maxlength="12"></div>
        <div class="modal-row">
          <label>Color</label>
          <div class="modal-color-row" id="et-presets">
            ${PRESET_COLORS.map(c => `<div class="color-preset${tier.color===c?' active':''}" style="background:${c}" data-c="${c}" onclick="pickPresetColor('${c}')"></div>`).join('')}
            <input type="color" id="et-color" value="${tier.color}">
          </div>
        </div>
        <div class="modal-row"><label>Tint Color</label><input type="color" id="et-text" value="${tier.text.startsWith('#') ? tier.text : '#ffffff'}"></div>
        <div class="modal-check-row">
          <input type="checkbox" id="et-exec" ${tier.isExec ? 'checked' : ''}>
          <label for="et-exec">Execution Rank</label>
        </div>
        <div class="modal-btns">
          <button onclick="closeModal()">Cancel</button>
          <button class="btn-danger btn-sm" onclick="deleteTier('${id}')">Delete</button>
          <button class="btn-primary" onclick="saveEditTier('${id}')">Save</button>
        </div>`;
      document.getElementById('et-color').addEventListener('input', () => document.querySelectorAll('#et-presets .color-preset').forEach(el => el.classList.remove('active')));
      openModal();
    }
    function pickPresetColor(c) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      document.getElementById('et-color').value = c;
      document.querySelectorAll('#et-presets .color-preset').forEach(el => el.classList.toggle('active', el.dataset.c === c));
    }
    function saveEditTier(id) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      const tier = getTier(id); if (!tier) { closeModal(); return; }
      tier.label  = document.getElementById('et-label').value.trim() || tier.label;
      tier.color  = document.getElementById('et-color').value;
      tier.text   = document.getElementById('et-text').value;
      tier.isExec = document.getElementById('et-exec').checked;
      closeModal(); syncPresetSel(); renderAll(); syncToSupabase();
    }
    function deleteTier(id) {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      allTiers = allTiers.filter(t => t.id !== id);
      activeTierIds = activeTierIds.filter(i => i !== id);
      poolItems.push(...(tierItems[id] || []));
      delete tierItems[id];
      closeModal(); syncPresetSel(); renderAll(); syncToSupabase();
    }

    function openManageTiers() {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      const modal = document.getElementById('modalBox'); modal.innerHTML = '';
      const title = document.createElement('div'); title.className = 'modal-title'; title.textContent = 'Manage Tiers'; modal.appendChild(title);
      const list = document.createElement('div'); list.className = 'tier-manage-list';
      function rebuildList() {
        list.innerHTML = '';
        getActiveTiers().forEach((tier, idx) => {
          const entry = document.createElement('div'); entry.className = 'tier-manage-entry';
          const swatch = document.createElement('div'); swatch.className = 'swatch'; swatch.style.background = tier.color;
          const lbl = document.createElement('div'); lbl.className = 'lbl'; lbl.textContent = tier.label;
          const btns = document.createElement('div'); btns.className = 'tier-manage-btns';
          if (tier.isExec) { const badge = document.createElement('span'); badge.className = 'exec-badge'; badge.textContent = 'EXEC'; btns.appendChild(badge); }
          const upBtn = document.createElement('button'); upBtn.className = 'btn-sm'; upBtn.textContent = '↑';
          upBtn.onclick = () => { if (idx > 0) { [activeTierIds[idx-1], activeTierIds[idx]] = [activeTierIds[idx], activeTierIds[idx-1]]; rebuildList(); } };
          const dnBtn = document.createElement('button'); dnBtn.className = 'btn-sm'; dnBtn.textContent = '↓';
          dnBtn.onclick = () => { if (idx < activeTierIds.length-1) { [activeTierIds[idx], activeTierIds[idx+1]] = [activeTierIds[idx+1], activeTierIds[idx]]; rebuildList(); } };
          const edBtn = document.createElement('button'); edBtn.className = 'btn-sm'; edBtn.textContent = '✎';
          edBtn.onclick = () => { closeModal(); openEditTier(tier.id); };
          btns.appendChild(upBtn); btns.appendChild(dnBtn); btns.appendChild(edBtn);
          entry.appendChild(swatch); entry.appendChild(lbl); entry.appendChild(btns); list.appendChild(entry);
        });
      }
      rebuildList(); modal.appendChild(list);
      const addTitle = document.createElement('div');
      addTitle.style.cssText = 'font-size:10px;color:hsl(var(--muted-foreground));text-transform:uppercase;letter-spacing:1px;padding-top:8px;border-top:1px solid hsl(var(--border))';
      addTitle.textContent = 'Add New Tier'; modal.appendChild(addTitle);
      const newRow = document.createElement('div'); newRow.style.cssText = 'display:flex;gap:6px;align-items:center;flex-wrap:wrap';
      const newLabel = document.createElement('input'); newLabel.type = 'text'; newLabel.id = 'tm-newlabel'; newLabel.placeholder = 'Label'; newLabel.style.cssText = 'flex:1;min-width:60px';
      const newColor = document.createElement('input'); newColor.type = 'color'; newColor.id = 'tm-newcolor'; newColor.value = '#888888';
      const newExecWrap = document.createElement('label'); newExecWrap.style.cssText = 'display:flex;align-items:center;gap:4px;font-size:11px;cursor:pointer';
      const newExecCb = document.createElement('input'); newExecCb.type = 'checkbox'; newExecCb.id = 'tm-newexec';
      newExecWrap.appendChild(newExecCb); newExecWrap.appendChild(document.createTextNode('Exec'));
      const addBtn = document.createElement('button'); addBtn.className = 'btn-primary btn-sm'; addBtn.textContent = '+ Add';
      addBtn.onclick = () => {
        const lbl = document.getElementById('tm-newlabel').value.trim(); if (!lbl) return;
        const color = document.getElementById('tm-newcolor').value;
        const isExec = document.getElementById('tm-newexec').checked;
        const brightness = parseInt(color.slice(1,3),16)*0.299 + parseInt(color.slice(3,5),16)*0.587 + parseInt(color.slice(5,7),16)*0.114;
        const text = brightness > 128 ? '#1a1a1a' : '#ffffff';
        const newId = 'custom_' + Date.now();
        allTiers.push({ id: newId, label: lbl, color, text, isExec });
        activeTierIds.push(newId);
        document.getElementById('tm-newlabel').value = ''; rebuildList();
      };
      newRow.appendChild(newLabel); newRow.appendChild(newColor); newRow.appendChild(newExecWrap); newRow.appendChild(addBtn); modal.appendChild(newRow);
      const btns = document.createElement('div'); btns.className = 'modal-btns';
      const doneBtn = document.createElement('button'); doneBtn.className = 'btn-primary'; doneBtn.textContent = 'Done';
      doneBtn.onclick = () => { closeModal(); syncPresetSel(); renderAll(); syncToSupabase(); };
      btns.appendChild(doneBtn); modal.appendChild(btns);
      openModal();
    }

    function openModal()  { document.getElementById('modalOverlay').classList.add('open'); }
    function closeModal() { document.getElementById('modalOverlay').classList.remove('open'); }
    document.getElementById('modalOverlay').addEventListener('click', e => { if (e.target === document.getElementById('modalOverlay')) closeModal(); });
    function escHtml(s) { return String(s||'').replace(/&/g,'&amp;').replace(/</g,'&lt;').replace(/>/g,'&gt;').replace(/"/g,'&quot;'); }

    function saveImage() {
      const s = document.createElement('script'); s.src = 'https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/html2canvas/1.4.1/html2canvas.min.js';
      s.onload = () => { html2canvas(document.getElementById('tierList'), { backgroundColor: '#1a1a1a', scale: 2, useCORS: true }).then(canvas => { const a = document.createElement('a'); a.download = 'tierlist.png'; a.href = canvas.toDataURL('image/png'); a.click(); }); };
      document.head.appendChild(s);
    }

    document.getElementById('itemType').addEventListener('change', function() {
      document.getElementById('itemLabel').style.display = (this.value !== 'text' && this.value !== 'image') ? 'block' : 'none';
      document.getElementById('itemInput').placeholder = this.value === 'text' ? 'Label...' : 'Paste URL...';
    });
    document.getElementById('itemInput').addEventListener('keydown', e => { if (e.key === 'Enter') addItem(); });
    document.getElementById('presetSel').addEventListener('change', function() {
      const v = this.value; if (v === 'custom') return;
      if (!PRESETS[v]) return;
      allTiers = JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(TIERS_BASE)); activeTierIds = [...PRESETS[v]]; renderAll(); syncToSupabase();
    });
    document.getElementById('colSel').addEventListener('change', function() { columns = parseInt(this.value); renderAll(); syncToSupabase(); });
    document.getElementById('bonusRevival').addEventListener('change', function() { revivalTint = this.checked; renderAll(); syncToSupabase(); });

    document.addEventListener('paste', e => {
      if (!isAdmin) return;
      const items = e.clipboardData?.items;
      if (!items) return;
      for (const item of items) {
        if (item.type.startsWith('image/')) {
          const file = item.getAsFile();
          const reader = new FileReader();
          reader.onload = ev => addItem({ dataUrl: ev.target.result });
          reader.readAsDataURL(file);
          return;
        }
      }
      const text = e.clipboardData.getData('text/plain').trim();
      if (!text) return;
      const active = document.activeElement;
      if (active && (active.tagName === 'INPUT' || active.tagName === 'TEXTAREA')) return;
      const isUrl = /^https?:\/\//.test(text);
      if (isUrl) {
        const isImg = /\.(jpg|jpeg|png|gif|webp|svg|avif)(\?|$)/i.test(text);
        addItem({ type: isImg ? 'image' : 'text', input: text, label: '' });
      } else {
        addItem({ type: 'text', input: text, label: '' });
      }
    });

    document.addEventListener('touchstart', e => {
      if (!e.target.closest('.tilt-wrapper')) document.querySelectorAll('.tilt-wrapper.is-tapped').forEach(w => { w.classList.remove('is-tapped'); const c = w.querySelector('.tl-item'); if (c) c.style.transform = 'rotateX(0deg) rotateY(0deg) scale3d(1,1,1)'; });
    }, { passive: true });

    document.getElementById('pool').dataset.tier = '__pool__';
    setupDrop(document.getElementById('pool'));

    loadRankingDat().then(() => {
      renderSavesList();
      initAuth();
      initDatabase();
    });
  </script>
  </body>
</html>
